It is not binding upon other</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">co-accused but such confessional statement when corroborated by independent evidence can also form the basis of conviction of other non-confessing accused.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nuruddin alias Shahabuddin and another Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 379.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 171— Responsibility of Police officer to produce witness during trial—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 492— Appointment of Public Prosecutor- Change of—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Responsibility of Investigating Police Officer does not end with the submission of charge-sheet. under section 173 Cr.P.C. on completion of investigation but continues till the conclusion of trial during which it is his duly to produce the prosecution witness. When there are persistent</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">allegations against the Public Prosecutor about his lack of interest and honesty in conducting the prosecution, the change of the Public Prosecutor becomes imperative in the interest of fair trial.</span><span lang="BN-BD" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-bidi-language: BN-BD;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Daily Star and Prothom Alo Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 135.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>172—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Case<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Diary of</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">investigation of Criminal Case— Not</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">a pubic document—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .25pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Case Diary maintained by Investigating Officer of a Criminal Case is not a public document as contemplated by section 172 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 and as such the Court cannot direct the Investigating officer to make part of Case diary public document by swearing affidavit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">But High Court Division can direct examination / re-examination of detenu by Medical Board and submit report on the allegation of torture.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Bangladesh represented by Secretary Ministry of Home Affairs and others Vs. Dr. Shamima Sultana Rita, </span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">7 <em>MLR(2002) (AD)140.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 11.05pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-bidi-language: BN-BD;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 173— Scope of further</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">investigation<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>at<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the instance of</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">accused</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Further Investigation may be made on the direction of Magistrate or Sessions Judge or superior Police Officer. But no further investigation can be made at the instance of an accused in order to exclude him from the charge sheet already submitted.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Alamgtr Siddique Buiyan Vs. The State and another, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 298.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .7pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 181— Jurisdiction of Court</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">to try offence under section 406 of the</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 1.7pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The offence under section 406 of the Penal Code, 1860 may be tried either by the Court in whose jurisdiction the money in question is received or by the court in whose jurisdiction the money so received is retained or denied as contemplated under section 181 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898.<em>Anwar Hossain and another Vs. the State and another, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 431.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 1.7pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.65pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 195— Case upon complaint from court</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Competent Court only can entertain a case upon a complaint from the court where the allegation in relation to the proceedings thereof are made.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Syed Ahmed Chowdhury Vs. Abdur Rashid Mridha and others, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 346.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.65pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 195— Complaint of Court in respect of certain offences—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 537— Irregularities curable</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Upazila Revenue Officer is not a Court and the mutation proceedings are not judicial proceedings. And as such section 195 of the Code of Criminal Procedure is not attracted in respect of use of forged document in the said proceedings. Therefore case started on police report is maintainable.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Abul Hossain (Md.) Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 290.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.65pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898-Section 195(l)(c)— Does not apply</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">to a case where photo copy of forged</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">document is produced</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.65pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The warrant of the law as contained in section 195(l)(c) of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 is that the Court in which the original forged document has been produced and given in evidence is required to send complaint in writing to the Court of competent jurisdiction whereupon only cognizance can be taken of the offence. This provision does not apply to a case where photocopy of the alleged forged document is produced. In such case private complaint is competent.<em>Abdul Gafur alias Khan Mia and others Vs. Md. Nurul Islam and the State, 8</em> <em>MLR (2004) (HC) 95.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 Section 195(l)(c)— Revenue officer dealing with mutation case is not a court and as such is not required to lodge complaint against forgery o document</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="Style3" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.4pt 12.5pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Revenue officer while dealing wit</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-bidi-language: BN-BD;">h</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> mutation case being not a court is no required under section 195(l)(c) of the Code of Criminal Procedure to lodge complaint against forgery of documents. In such case private complaint is maintainable. <em>Chitta Ranjan Das @ Chitta Ranjan Sinha Vs. Shashi Mohan Das and another, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 133.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 11.3pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.1pt 11.3pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 195(l)(c) and 476A— Complaint against filing and using false and fraudulent document before court— </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It is the duty of the Court to send complaint to the Magistrate of competent jurisdiction for prosecution for<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>filing<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and using fraudulent document m a proceeding before such court <em>Makhon Bora! and others Vs. Shaylendra NathMondal and others, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 161.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 5.3pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 195(2)— Revenue Officer dealing with mutation case is not a court—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 5.3pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.15pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Revenue Officer dealing with mutation case is not a court and as such there is no legal bar against private complaint in respect of forged deed produced in the mutation proceedings. <em>Shanti Ram Sarker Vs. The State and mother, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 233.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.15pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></em></p><p class="Style9" style="text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 12.25pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 200 and 202— Both the cases over same occurrence one started on police report and the other on complaint shall be tried simultaneously by the same court— No limitation for criminal case—</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="Style9" style="text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 12.25pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="Style9" style="margin: 0in 12.25pt 0.0001pt 13.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There is no limitation for lodging complaint in respect of criminal offence. Magistrate cannot dismiss the complaint merely because the same is belated one. In a case triable by court of Session, Magistrate is required to examine the witnesses and if prima facie case is made out he shall send the case to the court of session after taking cognizance. When over the same occurrence two cases-one on police report and the other on complaint are started<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>both the cases shall be tried simultaneously by the same court. Meanwhile during enquiry the further proceedings of the police case shall be kept stayed by the court of Session.</span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">A. Rob Munshi Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 104.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 6.5pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 200 and 247— Repeated complaint on self same occurrence is not maintainable—</span></strong></p><p class="Style3" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.45pt .25pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Though there is no legal bar against fresh complaint after the first one is disposed of due to default of the complainant, there should be limit to it. In entertaining such complaint Magistrate shall apply his judicial mind and must not act mechanically. Magistrate should stop entertaining repeated complaint one after another on the same allegation in order to prevent abuse of the process of the Court. <em>Habibur Rahman (Md.) Vs. Feroj Ahmed and others, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 131.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.9pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 202— Judicial inquiry— Presence <em><span style="letter-spacing: 1.5pt;">o' </span></em>Police Officer on behalf of accused police officers not permissible in law</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Police Regulation, 1943—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Regulation 24(a) and 29(d)— Are subservient to the Code of Criminal Procedure</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There is no provision of law requiring presence of Police Officer during judicial inquiry against accused police personnels. <em>Alena Akhter Khan and Moni Begum Vs. The State and others, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 215.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.4pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 236 and 237— Accused may be<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>convicted<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>for offence proved though not charged specifically for that—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 164 and 364— Confessional Statement and recording thereof—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Evidence Act, 1872—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 134— Conviction may be awarded on the basis of evidence of a solitary witness if found trustworthy</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .25pt .25pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It is well within the competence of the trial court to convict an accused for the offence proved during trial although he was not specifically charged with under the relevant section of the law as contemplated under section 236 and 237 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. Confessional statement-judicial or extra-judicial when found true and voluntary can well form the basis of conviction. Prosecution is not bound to produce each and every witness mentioned in the charge sheet. Abettor is also liable to the same sentence as the principal offender . </span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">State Vs. Md. Abdus Samad Azad and another, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 46.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 1.7pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 1.7pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 237 Cr.P.C— Punishment may be imposed for different offence when proved though not charged there for</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—When charge of murder committed with brutality is established the death penalty is appropriate. Where in a case mitigating circumstance exists alternative sentence of imprisonment for life would be the proper sentence Section 34 is attracted when the accused in furtherance of their common intention commit the murder. In case of section 34 participation in commission of offence is the constituent ingredient while section 109 is attracted where conspirncy and abetment in the commission of offence is done.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .5pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Accused may be convicted for the offence proved as provided under section 237Cr.P.C. even though the charge was not framed there for. <em>Ershad AH Sikdar and others Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 192.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 3.85pt 0in 0.0001pt 13.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>237— Error in framing charge when curable—</span></strong></p><p class="Style5" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 164— Statement of witness recorded under section 164— not substantive evidence— not legally acceptable evidence when the witness examined during trial gives a different story</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— </span></p><p class="Style5" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When charge is not properly framed with regard to specific offence, the accused cannot be convicted for the same. Abettor cannot be convicted for the offence for which the principal <strong><span style="mso-font-width: 10%;">I </span></strong>accused is not charged with. Statement of a witness recorded under section 164 Cr.P.C. is not substantive evidence and can not form the sole basis of conviction when the witness during her examination in trial gives a different story. Such statement can be used by the defence for contradiction<em> Azam (Md.) Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 299.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.95pt 0.0001pt 13.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 3.35pt 0.95pt 0.0001pt 13.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure 1898— Section 237 Cr.P.C— Punishment may be imposed for different offence when proved though not charged with—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 3.35pt 0.95pt 0.0001pt 13.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0.7pt 0in 0.0001pt 13.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When charge of murder committed with brutality is established the death penalty is appropriate. Where in a case mitigating circumstance exists alternative sentence of imprisonment for life would be the proper sentence.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 34 is attracted when the accused in furtherance of their common intention commit the murder. In case of section 34 participation in commission of offence is the constituent ingredient while section 109 is attracted where conspiracy and abetment in the commission of offence is done.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .5pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Accused may be convicted for the offence proved as provided under section 237Cr.P.C. even though the charge was not framed therefor. <em>Ershad AH Sikdar and others Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 192.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 4.55pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 4.55pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 238— Punishment for minor offence when found proved in a case of charge framed for major offence</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case where the charge for major offence falls but minor offence is proved in connection with the same occurrence the accused may well be punished for the minor offence even though no such charge was framed as provided under section 238 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.</span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Rajib Kamal Hassan and three others Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 70.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 239— Joinder of charges— offence committed in same transaction — Penal Code, 1860— Double murder- joinder of charge</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When offences are committed by same set of persons in the same place and time in the course of same transaction, they can be charged together and tried jointly as provided under section 239 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. <em>Delwar Hossain Khan Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (AD) 306.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 241A— Accused can not be discharged when the allegations are supported by materials on record—</span></strong></p><p class="Style3" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 3.35pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Trial Court is quite justified to frame charge under section 4(1) of the Ain Srinkhola Bignakari Aparadh (Druta Bicher) Ain, 2002 when the materials on record prima facie support the case to go for trial. Court is not required to scrutinise the adequacy or inadequacy of the evidence at this stage which can only be done during trial. Having regard to the position of law as above the High Court Division summarily rejected the application under section 435 and 439 Cr.P.C. seeking to interfere with the rejection of the application under section 241A Cr.P.C.</span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Haji Mohammad Selim and others Vs. State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 366.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.1pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 241A and 265C— Discharge of accused where cannot be made— on ground of misjoinder of charge-Special Powers Act, 1974— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span>25A— Counterfeiting currency notes— Penal Code, 1860— Section 498A— 498D— Counter­feiting currency notes— Joint trial of schedule and non-schedule offence-Permissibility of</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Though joinder of schedule and non-schedule offence in a trial is not usually permissible under the Special Powers Act, 1974 but where schedule and non-schedule offence such as that of section 25A of the Special Powers Act, 1974 and sections 498A-498D of the Penal Code fall in the same definition joint trial of schedule and non-schedule offence in such circumstances can not be held to be impermissible in law in view of the fact that the offence defined under both the law constitutes same offence. Discharge of accused on such ground cannot be claimed. <em>Ayub Ali alias Md. Aynb Ah and another Vs. The State, 6 MLR <span style="letter-spacing: -1.0pt;">(2001)</span> <span style="letter-spacing: -1.0pt;">(HC) </span>130.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 241A—Discharge of accused<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>on<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>plea of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>alibi— not permissible—</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Plea of alibi by way of defence can only be taken during trial subject to satisfactory proof thereof. At the time of framing charge the court or Magistrate has to see only if the prosecution has been able to establish prima-facie case against the accused to go for trial. Accused can not be discharged on plea of alibi at this stage. <em>Shah Alam Vs. The State and another, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 338.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">247—Dismissal of Complaint for non-appearance of Complainant—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Unless the case is fixed for hearing or is fixed for appearance of the complainant the case as a matter of course cannot be dismissed for non­appearance of the complainant when adjournment was sought for on medical ground Abdul Jabbar Howladar Vs. AH Akbar Howlader and another, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 70.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 249— Proceedings stopped </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">can well be revived—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 245— Release of accused under section 249 is not acquittal—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 4.5pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .7pt 0in .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When there are case and counter case over the same occurrence both the cases should be tried <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>simultaneously by the same court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Proceedings stopped under section 249 Cr.P.C. can well be revived since the release there under is neither acquittal nor discharge as provided under section 245 Cr.P.C. <em>Mosharraf Hossain Sheikh (Md.) Vs. Abdul Kader and others, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 235.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 265-C— Discharge of accused—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Accused may be discharged when charges appear to be groundless under section 265C of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898. In so doing the court must record the reasons therefor. Counter case is no ground for discharge of accused. Both the case and counter case should be tried simultaneously in accordance with law.<em>Terdousi Islam Vs. Nur Mohammad Khan and others, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 31.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1398— Section 265C-265D— Discharge of accused and framing of charge— Reasoning should be given in the case of former while no such reasoning is necessary in case of the latter</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Mere mentioning of the name of the accused in the F.I.R. and Police report ifso-facto shall not entitle the court to frame charge under section 265-D. When the charge appears groundless from the materials on record the accused shall be entitled to be discharged under section 265-C of the Code of Criminal Procedure. Court is not obliged to record detailed reasons while framing charge. But in case of discharge the court must record reasoning for so doing.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Taker Hossain Rushdi Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 83.</span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> <br/></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Section 265-C— Discharge of accused when there are not sufficient materials to proceed—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Section 265-D— Framing of charge when the court presume on the basis of materials that the accused committed the offence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">There is difference between 265-C and 265-D as to the requirement of recording reason. In the case of discharge the court has to record reasons for so doing. But in the case where charge is framed on the materials on record elaborate recording of reasons is not necessary.</span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Taker Hossain Rushdi Vs. The State, </span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">7 <em>MLR (2002) (AD) 116.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Sections 265B, 265-C, 265-D and 265-E</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">Hearing under all these sections need not be in separate session—</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">When the accused appears </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">or <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">brought before the court pursuant </span>to <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">section 205C, opening of the case </span>by <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">the prosecution, upon hearing the parties the framing of the charge </span>by <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">the court where accused is not discharged shall have to </span>be <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">done in the same session. No separate dates need </span>be <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">fixed for all the stages under sections 265B, 265C, 265D and 265E of the Code of Criminal Procedure, </span>1898.<em>Securities and Exchange Commission Vs. Abu Tyeb and 10 others, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 83.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> <br/></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>339C(4)—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Bail<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>may be granted when trial not concluded within statutory period.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Section 497 and 498— In case of non-bailable offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life bail may be granted on certain grounds.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Heinousness or grievousness by does not restrict the discretion of the court to grant bail. In a case of non-bailable offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life bail may be granted to an accused as contemplated under section 339C(4) of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 when trial could not be concluded within the statutory period. Moreover it is well within the discretion of the court to grant bail on certain grounds under section 497 and 498 Cr. P.C. Heinousness or grievousness by itself does not take away the discretion of the court.<em>Captain (Retd.) NurulHuda Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 53.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 342 and 364— Examination of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>accused-<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Legal requirements thereof— Not an idle formality—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">A Judge or a Magistrate while examining accused under section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure has to comply with provision of section 364 Cr.P.C. When material evidences such as the dying declaration of the victim and the confessional statements are not brought to the notice of the accused, this omission causes prejudice to the accused or in other words such examination is in no sense of the term an examination as contemplated under section 342 Cr.P.C which consequently rendered the conviction and sentence not sustainable in law.<em>State Vs. Kabez Molla and others, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 378.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 342— Examination of accused— legal implications— Delay in lodging FIR—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When satisfactorily explained— not fatal— Alibi taken during trial— Proof thereof</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">S</span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">ection 342 Cr.P.C. provides for an opportunity to the accused to explain his position in relation to the evidence brought on record against him. He may file documents which form part of his statement. He is not required to prove those document. Such statement of accused is not evidence within the meaning of section 3 of the Evidence Act, 1872.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Neither the prosecution nor the court can use such statement against the accused except for his benefit. Alibi taken by the accused during trial must be proved by him to the satisfaction of the Court.<em>Minhaz and another Vs. The State, </em>6 <em>MLR (2001) (AD) 166.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 13.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 4.5pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 342— Examination of the accused<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span>by<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span>the Court— Test</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Identification parade of suspect— Inordinate delay diminishes the evidentiary value</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure provides an opportunity to the accused to explain his position in relation to the incriminating materials brought on record while being examined by the trial court. This is not an idle formality. The court has to give due consideration to the statement of the accused. Non consideration of the material statements of the accused causes prejudice which vitiates the trial rendering ground for acquittal of the accused.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Inordinate delay in holding TI parade reduces the evidentiary value of identification of the suspects. When the witness had the opportunity to see the suspects after arrest and before holding the TI Parade, the identification of the suspect in such TI parade is of no legal value and can not form the basis of conviction particularly when allegation of enmity is there.<em>Ibrahim (Md.) and others Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 62.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 344— Case and counter case over the same occurrence shall be tried simultaneously by the same judge—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In order to avoid conflicting decision and other complications case and counter case over the same occurrence shall be tried simultaneously by the same judge as contemplated under section 344 Cr.P.C. <em>Tarek Shamsul Khan alias Himu and others Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC)142.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>345—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Compounding of offence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">As provided under section 345 of the Code of Criminal Procedure offence under section 325 of the Penal Code may be compounded by the person to whom hurt is caused. <em>Ynsuf Ali and others Vs. The State and another, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 352.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 369—Provides for correction of clerical error—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Once the judgment is signed and pronounced this cannot be altered or reviewed by the same judge except correcting the clerical error as provided under section 369 Cr.P.C. Order 47 rule 1 of the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908 does not apply to the criminal proceedings. <em>Manjuara Khatnn (Most.) Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (AD) 31.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 374— Confirmation of death sentence and the liability of husband </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">to explain circumstance under which lis wife was murdered—Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 302— Charge of murder and the proof thereof—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Charge need not always be proved by ocular evidence. Circumstantial evidence unerringly pointing at the guilt of the accused can well form the basis of conviction. Husband has heavy liability to explain the circumstance under which his wife was murdered when they were living in the same house at the time of the occurrence. In the absence of any satisfactory explanation from the husband, the medical evidence together with the ascension of the accused immediately after the occurrence and the chain of other attending circumstance unerringly pointing at the guilt of the convict-accused the learned judges of the High Court Division having found the conviction and sentence perfectly justified confirmed the sentence of death.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">State Vs. Md. Delwar Hossain Faraji condemned prisoner, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 375.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 417-Criminal Appeal cannot be dismissed for default—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">A criminal appeal once admitted for hearing shall be decided on merit. It cannot be dismissed for default. The presence of the appellant at the time of hearing is not requirement of law.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Kamal Mia (Md.) Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 305.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 417(1)(3)— Appeal against acquittal in complaint case—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Limitation Act, 1908— Applicability of article 157—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">In case of appeal against acquittal in a complaint case the limitation is 60 days as provided under section 417(1)(3) of the Code of Criminal Procedure. But in case of appeal against acquittal in a case initiated on police report the limitation is 6 months under article 157 of the Limitation Act.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Dr. M.A. Mazed and others Vs. Government of Bangladesh represented by Solicitor, 9 MLR (2004) (AD) 164.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in 2.65pt .0001pt 13.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Code of Criminal Procedure. 1898— Section 431— Abatement of appeal on the death of appellant</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 10.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Appeal against imprisonment abates on the death of the appellant. But it does not abate against the sentence of fine which shall be continued notwithstanding the death of the appellant for realization. The legal representatives of the deceased appellant are allowed to proceed with the appeal. <em>Taibur Rahman Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 336.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 10.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 435 and 439— Enhancement of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>sentence—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Proportionality of sentence with gravity of offence</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 10.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The purpose of the law in criminal jurisprudence is that sentence shovild be proportionate to the gravity of offence and shall serve as deterrent to the potential offenders for maintaining law and order situation in society. Too light a sentence in relation to gravity of offence makes the administration of criminal justice ridiculous. <em>Nuriin Nabi (Mohammed) Vs. Sahin Alam alias maktn and others, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 218.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 10.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 10.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 436— Session Judge cannot direct Magistrate to take cognizance of any offence against any accused—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 10.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 561A— Quashment of proceedings on ground of abuse of the process of court</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 10.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sessions Judge can direct further inquiry but he can not direct Magistrate to take cognizance of an offence against any accused in exercise of powers under section 436, Cr.P.C. High Court Division can quash the proceedings under section 561A Cr.P.C. on ground of abuse of the process of court.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Basiran Bezua (Mst.) Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 224.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898-Section 439—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Informant is quite competent to bring application under section 439 when the state fails to take any step, against the order of discharge of an accused in a Session case..<em>Abdur Rahman Kha (Md.) Vs. The Stakl and another, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 294.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 439— Direction for further investigation upon narajee petition-</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">On Narajee petition disclosing material evidence direction for further investigation by the police can well be given treating the same as fresh complaint. There is nothing wrong in such direction.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Saidur Rahman Shahid (Md.) Vs. Thel State, 10 MLR (2005) (AD) 29.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 476 and 195(1)— Lodging complaint<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>by<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Public Servant-Cognizance by the Magistrate</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Process Server submitted report to the Senior Assistant judge about the offence committed by the petitioner while he was executing the decree of the court. The Senior Assistant Judge after examining the report and being satisfied sent the report to the magistrate of competent jurisdiction who thereupon took cognizance of the offence under section 183, 186 and 188of the Penal Code. The apex court held there was sufficient compliance with the requirement of law. <em>A.K.M. Samsnddin alias Kalam doctor and another Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (AD) 278.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 491— Power of the High Court Division to direct release of minor<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>victim<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>girl<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>from judicial custody.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Dispute as to the age and custody of minor girl can be decided pending trial of the case <em>relying </em>upon the school certificate and statement of the parents in preference to the opinion of the Radiologist. High Court Division also can similarly direct release of the minor victim girl from judicial custody in an independent proceedings under section 491 Cr.P.C. and to hand over her to the custody of her father.<em>Arun Karmakar Vs. The State represented by the Deputy Commissioner; Satkhira and another, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 162.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 491— Custody of victim minor girl- Determination of age— Jurisdictions of High Court Division to issue writ of Habeas corpus</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Victim minor girl who is not an accused cannot be kept in custody for indefinite period. She should be given to the custody of her father if a minor or should be released either with or without bond if she is a major. High Court Division can interfere under section 491 Cr.P.C. notwithstanding the pending case.</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Arun Karmakar Vs. <em>The State and another, 7 MLR (2002) (AD) 82.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>491—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Habeas Corpus-Power of the High Court Division— Special Powers Act, 1974— Section 3— Preventive detention and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>grounds<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>thereof-<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>to be specific and definite</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Liberty of movement is a fundamental right of a citizen which is guaranteed by the Constitution. Unless there is any compelling situation no citizen can be put under preventive detention. Grounds for preventive detention must be specific and definite as to prejudicial activities defined under section 3 of the Special Powers Act, 1974 so that the detenu can make an effective representation before the authority; otherwise order of preventive detention passed in colorable exercise of power shall not be sustainable in the eye of law.<em>Afzal Hossain (Md.) Vs. Secretary M/O Home Affairs and others, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 142.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 491— Writ of Habeas corpus-Constitution of Bangladesh— Article 102 (2) (b) (i)— Infringement of fundamental rights—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Under section 491 of the Code either the detenu himself or a third person on his behalf can invoke the jurisdiction of the High Court Division challenging the legality of detention. But under article 102(2)(b)(i) of the Constitution only the aggrieved person may apply. District Magistrate or Additional District Magistrate has no jurisdiction to order de. mtion of a person in the Metropolitan Area where the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate can pass such order. The authority while ordering detention must act judicially and not arbitrarily.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Anwar Hossain (Md.) and others Vs. The State and others, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 385.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.1pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>492— Power of the Government<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>to<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>appoint Public prosecutor—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Government is empowered under section 492 of the Code of Criminal Procedure 1898 to appoint public prosecutor. Such appointment depends upon the satisfactory performance and confidence as in the case between a litigant and a lawyer. Indefinite<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>allegations<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>leading to termination of appointment does not constitute stigma warranting interference therewith by the court in writ jurisdiction. Termination of appointment of public prosecutor without show cause notice is not violative of the principle of natural justice.<em>Secretary Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs and others Vs. Md. Borhan uddin and others,9 </em></span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><em>MLR (2004) (AD) 349.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898-Section 492— Appointment of Public Prosecutor—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Government has the sole authority to appoint public Prosecutor and also terminate his appointment as and when it is found expedient to conduct case in court of session. Neither the informant nor any witness has any locus standi to challenge the termination of appointment of a public prosecutor.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">S.M. Jillur Rahman Vs. Government of Bangladesh represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs, 9 MLR (2004) (AD) 198.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 493— Anticipatory bail can be granted in exceptional cases</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Where there is strong apprehension that the accused petitioners will be subjected to harassment after arrest in a case initiated at the instance of the police and their bail petition would not be dealt with in accordance with law the accused petitioners are granted anticipatory bail.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Marnfa Siddique @ Boby and others Vs. State represented by the Deputy Commissioner, Dhaka, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 235.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 494— Withdrawal from prosecution with the consent o£ the Court— Court's power is discretionary— Such discretion has to be exercised judiciously—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Decisi</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">on of the Government to withdraw from prosecution against any accused must be based on reason to be recorded in the order of withdrawal. To accord consent to such withdrawal is the discretion of the trial court and such discretion has to be exercised judiciously and not mechanically as a matter of routine.
