The apex court discouraged withdrawal from prosecution when the accused concerned was still absconding. <em>State represented by Solicitor, Government of Bangladesh Vs. Md. Amir Hamza, 10 MLR (2005). (AD) 61.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 494—Withdrawal of Prosecution with consent of the Court</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Power of the Court where consent of the court is the legal necessity for withdrawal from prosecution has to be exercised judiciously and not mechanically as contemplated by section 10(4) of the Criminal Law Amendment Act, 1958 read with section 494 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898.<em>Loskar Mohammad Mostain Billah Vs. The State, </em>7 <em>MLR (2002) (HC) 265.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 497— Bail cannot be granted to an accused involved with direct complicity in offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case of murder where apparent complicity of the accused is evident from the F.I.R Charge sheet and other materials on record, the accused is not entitled to bail. Grant of bail to such an accused in disregard of the settled principle of law of bail by improper exercise of judicial discretion is illegal and is aside by the apex Court. <em>State Vs. FaisalAlamAnsari, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 51.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 497(1)— Grant of bail on ground of illness—Not always an absolute rule— Section 339C(4)— When trial s not concluded within statutory period accused is entitled to bail—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Working days of a court are to be counted taking into account the days on which the judge holds the court—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case of grave offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life bail to the accused may be refused even on ground of serious illness. The Court in that case can direct for arranging proper treatment of the accused. Right to be enlarged on bail in a case of non-bailable offence where trial could not be concluded within statutory period cannot be claimed as a matter of right. This right as provided under section 339C (4) of the Code of Criminal Procedure. 1898 is subject to the discretion of the Court which in appropriate case can refuse bail by showing reasons in writing. <em>Nurul Islam Monzoor Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 194.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><strong>Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 497 and 498</strong>— Bail granted by the Sessions judge under section 497 cannot be cancelled except on ground of misuse of privilege of bail-Bail granted by the Sessions judge under section 498 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 before arrest can be cancelled by the High Court Division if it is found that there was no reasonable ground for granting such ball. But when bail to the accused in custody is granted under section 497 Cr.P.C. by the Sessions Judge it can only be cancelled on the ground of abuse of the privileges of bail under sub-section(5) of section 497 Cr.P.C. and not otherwise. <em>Momtaz Begum Vs. The State &amp; others, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 166.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 498— Cancellation of bail and remedy thereafter—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">State prosecutor usually can seek for cancellation of bail of an accused on appropriate grounds. When the state does not come up, the private complainant also can seek for cancellation of bail. Against cancellation of bail revision lies under section 439 and not under section 498 Cr.P.C.</span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Mohasin AH Pramanik Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 186.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 9.1pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 498— Bail in a wife killing case___</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-indent: 9.1pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When there are incriminating materials on record such as FIR, inquest report and the post mortem examination report pointing at the guilt of the accused husband, bail of the accused husband is refused by the High Court Division at the time when the trial is pending before the trial court.<em>Azam Reza Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 138.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 498— Bail of accused on similar footing with other accused granted bail may also be allowed on similar consideration—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case where some accused are granted bail, the other accused of similar footing are also entitled to be granted the privilege of bail on similar consideration. <em>Jashimuddin Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 175.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 498— Grant of bail in non-bailable offence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Arms Act, 1878—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 19A— Bail of accused—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Upon rejection repeated bail petitions are permissible. So is the case with appeal against rejection of bail petition—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When investigation could not be completed within the specified time and when the accused is in custody for long time, the accused in such case of non-bailable offence may be granted bail as provided under sub-section (4) of section 339C of Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Repeated bail petition is permissible after the rejection of former ones. The same is the position of law with regard to appeal against repeated rejection of bail petition.<em>Khairul Alam (Md.) alias Masum Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 309.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 498— Both High Court Division and Sessions Judge have concurrent jurisdiction to entertain bail petition—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 0in .0001pt 10.55pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The usual practice is that though both the High Court Division and <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">Court </span>of Session have concurrent jurisdiction to entertain bail petition, the lower court has to be moved first. But this is not inviolable biblical rule. In appropriate case the High Court Division can directly entertain bail petition of an accused in custody when the interest of justice so demands.<em>State represented by the Deputy Commissioner, Dhaka Vs, Md. Nurul Islam @ Babul, 9 MLR (2004) (AD) 237.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—Section 498— Grant of bail in non-bailable offence—Section 167(5)— Long delay in completion of investigation—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Long delay in completion of investigation may render ground for granting bail to the accused in case of non-bailable offence. <em>Mashiur Rahman (Md.) @ Kana Babul Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 356.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1S98—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 517(1)— Confiscation of goods/property connected with the offence by court or tribunal on conclusion of trial—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Customs Act, 1969—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 15 and 16— Customs Authority is empowered to confiscate goods brought into Bangladesh in contravention of prohibition</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Since the Customs Authority is empowered to detain and confiscate goods brought into Bangladesh in contravention of prohibition he is not required to obtain permission of the Court or tribunal, as the case may be, for such confiscation pursuant to the relevant provisions of the Customs Act, 1969.<em>Omar Sharif Khan (Md.) Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 252.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 526— Transfer of criminal case by High Court Division</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Unless there is reasonable apprehension of not getting fair trial in the court concerned a case can not be transferred from one court to another. In case of inter-District transfer there must exist situation of grave nature. <em>Shahjahan Faraji and nnother Vs. The State, 7 MLR (1002) (HC) 420..</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 539B— Local inspection of the place of occurrence by Magistrate or Judge</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 15.35pt 0in .0001pt 11.05pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">For the purpose of appreciating properly the evidence and nature of offence, a magistrate or a judge at any stage of trial or enquiry may inspect the place of occurrence and make recommendation as to his opinion which shall form part of the record. During the preliminary enquiry there is no proceedings as yet before the court which can be quashed.</span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Zafariillah (Md.) Vs. Abu Bakar Siddique and others, </span></em><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">7 </span></strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">MLR (2002) (AD) 293.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.9pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 540— Court's power to call any person to be examined as witness at any stage of trial—</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.9pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Court has unfettered power under section 540 of the Code of Criminal Procedure to call any person to be examined as witness at any stage of trial or inquiry if it appears essential for just decision of the case before it, no matter whether his statement was recorded under section 161 Cr.P.C. or not. Question of further investigation in relation therewith is absolutely immaterial.</span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Ayub Ah Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HO 187.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.9pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Sectin 540— Recalling prosecution witness for farther examination—</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.9pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">In the interest of justice prosecution witness may be re-called as provided under section 540 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 before conclusion of the trial.<em>Kazi AH Zahir alias Elin and others Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 254.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 561A— Quashment of proceedings—Section 247— Acquittal of accused and subsequent fresh case on self­same allegations</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Subsequent fresh case upon an F.I.R lodged after the acquittal of the accused under section 247 Cr.P.C in a complaint case is not barred. When prima-facie offence is disclosed in the F.I.R the proceedings started thereon can not be quashed merely on the ground that the accused was acquitted under section 247 Cr.P.C in the previous complaint case.<em>Ahmed Mollique and others Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 297.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—Section 561A— Quashment of conviction and sentence—Penal Code, 1860—Section 385— Charge of extortion— Proof thereof—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Charge of extortion against the convict—petitioner was proved by satisfactory evidence. The convict-petitioner remained absconding during the whole trial after his release on bail. The contention that the neighbors were not examined is no ground for quashment of the conviction and sentence. <em>Abdullah-Al-Mohmud @ Ripon Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 259.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 561A— Quashment of proceedings— Amendment of procedural law unless contrary intention is expressly provided takes retrospective effect—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Unless there is apparently non­disclosure of any offence from the F.I.R. charge sheet and other materials on record or any legal bar against such proceedings or continuance of such proceedings is an abuse of the process of court, inherent jurisdiction Linder section 561A Cr.P.C. for quashing the proceedings cannot be invoked. When prima-facie offence is disclosed from the records there cannot be quashment of the proceedings. The court while exercising power under section 561A Cr.P.C cannot weigh the evidence which can only be done during trial by the trial court. <em>Shamtm Hossatn (Group Captain Retd) Vs. State and another, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 60.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Code</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> of Criminal Procedure, 1898—Section 561A— Quashment of proceedings— Failure of the accused to pay the price of goods does not constitute criminal offence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a business transaction where the accused failed to pay the price of potato supplied on credit it is a civil liability and as such the criminal proceedings instituted under section 406 and 420 of the Penal Code being the abuse of the process of the court is quashed.<em>Abdur Ronf alias Nayan (Md.) Vs. The State, </em>6 MLR (2001) (HC) 37.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure 1898— Section 561A/439— Setting aside charge—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Where the acts of a person constitute both civil and criminal offence, there is no legal bar to prosecute both civil and criminal proceedings against him. To stay the criminal proceedings till disposal of the civil suit will frustrate the purpose of the proceedings and defeat the intention of the law. And as such the High Court Division declined to interfere with the framing of the charge under section 406 and 420 of the Penal Code. <em>Abul Hossatn Mallick (Alhaj) Vs. Noorjahan Mallick Baby, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 39.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 561A and section 439—Second revision does not lie against decision of the 1st revision—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In appropriate case second revisional application may be converted into one under section 561A Cr. P.C</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">No Naraji Petition lies against charge sheet already filed. Person who is neither an informant nor a witness nor a person interested in the criminal proceeding has no locus standi to file naraji petition. No Naraji petition is maintainable seeking reinvestigation which is not permissible in law.<em>Abdul Mannan Sarker Vs. Abdul Khaleque and another, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 390.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 561A— Quashment of proceeding under section 406 and 420 of the Penal Code when no offence is disclosed— Request does not constitute false representation—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Supply of wheat on request on credit is a business transaction and the dispute arising therefrom is a civil liability. Unless there is initial deception, inducement on false representation, the delivery of wheat’s on credit and mere issue of a cheque which is dishonoured for want of sufficient fund do not constitute offence under section 406 and 420 of the Penal Code. When the allegations made in the complaint do not discloseany offence the proceedings drawn thereon being abuse of the process of the court is liable to be quashed.<em>Motaleb Hassain (Md.) Vs. The State &amp; another, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 168.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 561A— Quashment of proceeding for preventing abuse of the process of court</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Allegation made in the F.I.R. and charge sheet having disclosed no offence the proceedings under section 409 read with section 5(2) of the Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947 are quashed with a view to preventing the abuse of the process of Court.<em>Shokrana (Md.) Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 180.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 561A— Quashment of proceedings to prevent the abuse of the process of court—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section— 406 and 420— Loan money does not constitute offence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Unless there is inducement and entrustment loan taken for business purpose and failure or refusal to repay the same is a civil liability and does not constitute offence punishable under section 406 and 420 of the Penal Code. Therefore the proceedings being abuse of the process of Court are quashed. <em>Abdul Mannan </em>Sarker <em>(Md.) Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 279</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 516A— Custody of seized article- Power of Magistrate</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The article here the vessel seized should be given to the custody of the person who was in possession thereof when the offence was committed in relation thereto. Magistrate cannot decide ownership of the vessel. <em>Omar Ali (Md.) Vs. Abdul Malek and another, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 372.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 561A</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When proceedings are ex-facie illegal, quashment thereof is the appropriate remedy. No relief which is likely to affect the other side can be granted in a summary way without hearing the other side which is grossly violative of the principle of natural justice and is not sustainable in law. <em>Khorshida Begum and another Vs. Colam Mostafa and others, 7 MLR (2002) (AD) 46.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>561A—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Quashment ofproceedings not warranted when there exist no appropriate ground— Cruelty<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>to <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Women (Deterrent Punishment) Ordinance, 1983— Section 4— Offence to be tried by Special Tribunal. Special Powers Act, 1974— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 27— Taking cognizance on police report—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Court can take cognizance under proper section of law even where Police mentioned wrong number of section—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sessions Judge cannot direct Special Tribunal to take cognizance. Special Tribunal is empowered by law to take or not to take cognizance of offence where appropriate. Where the Police makes wrong noting of section of law the Tribunal can well take cognizance thereon under proper section of law. The proceedings cannot be quashed only on such ground.<em>Alauddin </em>Vs <em>The State, </em>7 <em>MLR (2002) (HC) 257.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>561A—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Quashment of proceedings Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881— Section 138— Case against offence for<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span>issuing<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span>cheque which is dishonored has to be filed within statutory perio</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">d</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The case initiating criminal proceedings shall be filed within the statutory period prescribed there for. Where no steps are taken within the time specified under section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881, the cause of action unlike in other situation for prosecution goes by default or the right accruing there under is barred by limitation. This special remedy can be availed of only when steps are taken within prescribed time.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Otherwise the criminal proceedings being not sustainable in law are liable to be quashed. In such a case alternative remedy is available in civil court. <em>Abdus Salam Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 270.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898-Section 561A— Quashment of proceeding - When not permissible-Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881— Section 138— Does not bar remedy under other laws</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the offence is clearly disclosed in the F.I.R. or in the complaint, the proceedings cannot be quashed. Since the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881 does not bar further remedy, the suit for recovery of money is maintainable notwithstanding the case instituted under the Negotiable Instrument Act. Moreover it is permissible under the law that charge may be amended at any time before pronouncement of judgment. <em>Moniruzzaman (Md.) Vs. A.N.M. Deydar-E-Alam and others, 7 MLR (2002) </em>(HC) 423.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898-Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>561A— Quashment of proceedings—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, I860— Section 420— Ingredients constituting the offence</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the offence under section 420 of the Penal Code, 1860 prima facie is disclosed in the petition of complaint the proceedings thereon cannot be quashed under section 561A Cr. P.C. on the plea of the transaction being civil in nature. <em>Fouzia Begum @ Rina and others Vs. Md. Azizul Bari and another, <u>8 MLR (2003) (AD) 63.</u></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 561A— Conviction and sentence passed on the basis of material evidence on record in presence of the convict petitioner cannot be quashed.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 5.75pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Section 24— Provides for appeal against conviction and sentence within 30 days.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When provisions of appeal under the special law with special limitation are available application under section <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">561A </span>Cr.P.C. for quashment of conviction and sentence does not lie.<em>Sharifa Begum @ Sharu Bibi Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 239.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 561A- Proceedings in which the dispute is of civil nature arising out of business transaction—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, I860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 406/420— Where the initial intention of cheating is absent, prosecution under section 420 does not lie—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Dispute relating to claim of payment of outstanding dues arising from long business transaction is of civil nature which can be decided in civil suit. Criminal proceedings thereon being abuse of the process of the court are quashed.<em>Dehvar Hossain Soiudagar (Alhaj) Vs. The State represented by the Deputy Commissioner Chittagong and others, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 183.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>561A—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Quashment of conviction and sentence</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division in exercise of its inherent power under section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure can quash the conviction and sentence only when the trial was held without jurisdiction, there was no offence constituted or it was a case of no evidence. <em>Delower Hossain @ AH Hossain Bhuiyan Vs. The State, 8 MLR </em>(2003) <em>(HC) 252.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>561A—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Quashment of proceedings on ground of abuse of the process of the Court—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947— Section 5(1)(2)— Criminal intention is the prerequisite—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In the absence of criminal intention no offence punishable under section 5(2) of the Prevention of Corruption Act is constituted. When certain acts are done collectively following the rules of procedure, no criminal intention can be inferred. Therefore when no offence is constituted the criminal proceedings initiated thereon being abuse of the process of court is liable to the quashed. <em>Begum Khaleda Zia Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 308.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>561A—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Quashment of conviction and sentence not based onlegal evidence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The onus lies upon the prosecution to prove the charge by legal evidence. Conviction and sentence which is not based on any legal evidence is liable to be quashed or set aside.<em>Aslam alias Md. Aslam Vs. the State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 420.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 561A— Quashment of proceeding when not warranted—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Delay in conclusion of trial is no ground for quashment of proceedings—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Except in case of extra-ordinary circumstance<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>generally<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>delay in conclusion of trial does not constitute ground for quashment of proceedings.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Investigation of offences under the Prevention of Corruption <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Act, 1947 by Assistant Inspector of BAC does not become vitiated and as such the proceedings based thereon cannot be qviashed for such ground.<em>Government of Bangladesh represented by Solicitor, Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs Vs. Md. Amjad All Mridha and others, 9 MLR (2004) (AD) 231.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>561A—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Quashment of proceedings on ground of abuse of the process of the Court— Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881— Section 138 and 141— Complaint when to be lodged—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Cheque can be presented to the Bank for payment within 6(six) months from the date of issue. Complaint shall have to be lodged within one month of the date of the cause of action arising from the failure of the drawer of the cheque incompliance with the notice issued by the drawee within 15(fifteen) days after the cheque was returned being dishonoured. When the complaint does not satisfy the above requirements and does not disclose cause of action, the proceeding is quashed being abuse of the process of the court. <em>Nizamaddin Mahmood Vs. Abdal Hamid Bhuiyan and another, 9 MLR (2004) (AD) 299.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section 561A— Order of acquittal cannot be quashed under section 561A Cr.P.C.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">High Court Division in exercise of powers under section 435 and 439 Cr.P.C. can examine the legality of an order of acquittal but it cannot quash order of acquittal under section 561A Cr.P.C. <em><span style="letter-spacing: -1.0pt;">Rezia</span> Khatun Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 232.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>561A—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Quashment of proceeding on ground of abuse of the process of court.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Statement of an accused made to the police is not evidence against the co-accused. Proceedings based on such statement being abuse of the process of the Court are liable to be quashed. <em>Alhaj Moulana M.A. Mannan Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 238.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure 1898—Section 561A— Quashment of proceedings—Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 418— Making licencing agreement on unsolicited offer does not constitute offence under section 418—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 5(2)—Criminal misconduct— constituent elements—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the allegations do not constitute offence under section 418 of the Penal Code read with section 5(2) of the Prevention of Corruption Act the proceedings initiated thereon being abuse of the process of the court are quashed.<em>Mohammad Nasim and another Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 364.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 561A— Proceedings being abuse of the process of the court are liable to be quashed—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 409/109— Misappropriation by criminal breach of trust—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 5(2)— Offence of criminal misconduct by abuse of official position—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case where the Minister and the Secretary acted merely on the recommendation of tender committee, they are not liable for any commission of offence, if any, committeed by the members of the tender committee. When no offence is disclosed either in the FIR or in the charge sheet, the proceedings initiated thereon being abuse of the process of the court Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 2.9pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 561A— Application for quashment of conviction and sentence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Santrash Mulak Aparadh Daman Ain, 1992—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 2(2) (gha) (cha)— Sentence of imprisonment for life is modified<br/></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Convict-petitioner did not prefer appeal against the conviction and sentence within the statutory period of limitation. Thereafter he filed an application under section 561A Cr.P.C. for quashment of the conviction and sentence which was rejected. Appellate Division while disposing of the petition for leave to appeal modified the sentence of imprisonment for life into one for rigorous imprisonment for 10(ten) years.<em>Jahangir Alam (Md.) alias Zakir Vs. The state, 10 MLR (2005) (AD) 335.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>561A—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Quashment of proceedings when the same is abuse of the process of the Court—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— Section 107 and 109— Abetment of commission of offence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Unless the ingredients as enumerated under section 107 of the Penal Code are fotind present there cannot be an offence of abetment punishable Linder section 109 of the Code. Mere request to do something does not constitute offence of abetment and as such proceedings drawn therefor being the abuse of the process of court is liable to be quashed. <em>Abdur Rahman Dhali and others Vs. Th State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 108.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 561A— Quashment of proceedings or conviction and sentence can only be made on certain well settled principles and not otherwise</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">.—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 102— Conditions of search need not be strictly complied with when incriminating articles are recovered from the body of the accused on search—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Lack of corroboration does not mean lack of legal evidence. Absconding accused is not legally entitled to insist upon corroborative evidence. Evidence of Official witness when found reliable can well form the basis of conviction.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When there is a case of no evidence, or any case not disclosing any offence or any legal bar, the proceedings or the conviction and sentence which do not suffer from any legal infirmity, can not be quashed. <em>Ayub AH (Md.) Vs. Md. Abdul Khaleque and another, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 192.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 561A— Quashment of proceeding on ground of illegality and lack of jurisdiction—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 339D— Since omitted there is no scope to revive proceedings stopped under section 339C—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Proceedings ended upon final report by the police can be reinitiated by filing naraji petition or by fresh complaint or by setting aside the same under section 435 and 439 Cr. P.C.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">After the omission of section 339D by the Code of Criminal Procedure (Amendment) Act, 1992 there is no scope to revive the proceedings stopped under section 339C. The impugned proceedings having been so revived the High Court Division quashed the same as being illegal and without jurisdiction. <em>Abul Kashem Bagoja and others Vs. State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 354.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Criminal trial- Nature of evidence-Where enmity between parties exists corroboration<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>by independent witness in required.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Where admittedly enmity between the parties exists, the rule of prudence in a criminal trial dictates that the court should ask for corroboration by independent witness even though there is no hard and fast rule that the evidence of partisan witness should always be discarded.<em>AllafHossain and others Vs. The State, 7 <span style="letter-spacing: -1.0pt;">MLR'</span> (2002) (HC) 189.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Criminal<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Trial-<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>When<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>part of evidence is disbelieved other part of</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 3.85pt 0in 0.0001pt 10.3pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">it may be accepted—There is no legal bar in a criminal trial when one part of evidence is disbelieved, to accept the remaining part which appears to be true and reliable in the attending circums­tances.<em>Hazrat Khan @ Hazrat Ali Khan Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 247.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 3.85pt 0in 0.0001pt 10.3pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898— Cancellation of bail on ground of misuse of the privilege</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 3.85pt 0in 0.0001pt 10.3pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When there is admittedly enmity between the parties due to political rivalry and the allegations of misuse of the privilege of bail are not established by any substantive * materials, anticipatory bail granted earlier can not be cancelled. <em>Haft Mohammad Salim and others Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 306.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Constitution of Bangladesh— Article 102- Maintainability of writ petition seeking declaration that the order of conviction and sentence passed by Special Tribunal is without jurisdiction— Special Powers Act, 1974— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span>30</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span><strong>Appeal against judgment and order of conviction and sentence—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Order of conviction and sentence which is not based on evidence on record is no judgment and order in the eye of law and the Tribunal has no jurisdiction to pass any such order of conviction and sentence. In a case where the Special Tribunal passed judgment and order of conviction and sentence without any legal evidence on record, such order of conviction and sentence can be declared illegal and passed without jurisdiction in writ petition although the petitioner could not prefer appeal against the same under section 30 of the Special Powers Act, 1974 in the circumstance beyond control. <em>Alam Hossain @ Ibrahim Vs. Government of Bangladesh and others, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 13.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Constitution of Bangladesh— Article 102 (2) (b) (i)— Infringement of fundamental rights—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Under section 491 of the Code either the detenu himself or a third person on his behalf can invoke the jurisdiction of the High Court Division challenging the legality of detention. But under article 102(2) (b)(i) of the Constitution only the aggrieved person may apply.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">District Magistrate or Additional District Magistrate has no jurisdiction to order detention of a person in the Metropolitan Area where the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate can pass such order. The authority while ordering detention must act judicially and not arbitrarily. <em>Anwar Hossain (Md.) and others Vs. The State, and others, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 385.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Constitution of Bangladesh—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Article 103(3)— Leave to appeal-not granted-when no legal infirmity or case of misreading of evidence on record could be pointed out—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">High Court Division upon proper appreciation of evidence on record consisting of material contradictions as to the time, place and manner of the occurrence and the eye witnesses giving conflicting accounts of the occurrence and the witnesses having found not reliable, set aside the conviction and sentence of the convict-appellants. The leave to appeal in the facts and circumstances of the case, has been refused.<em>The State Vs. Nasir Ahmed @ Nasimddin and another, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 242.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Constitution of Bangladesh— Article 105</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <strong>Review of judgment of the Appellate Division—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Except in a case of any legal infirmity occasioning failure of justice the Appellate Division does not in the name of review of its judgment, reopen a finally concluded matter leading to a situation of sitting over its own decision as a court of appeal and rewrite a judgment afresh, a proposition which is being consistently held unacceptable. <em>Babul Mtah (Md.) Vs. The State and others, </em>6 MLR (2001) (AD) 239.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Constitution of Bangladesh— Article 105- Review of judgment onground of error apparent on the face of record—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Unless there is error apparent on the face of record occasioning miscarriage of justice review of judgment can not be made.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.85pt 0in .0001pt 10.3pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">That the lawyer could not raise certain point at the time of trial or hearing is no ground for review of judgment. <em>Mukul Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (AD) 276.</em></span></p><p> </p><p> </p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">  </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 10.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 10.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> </span></p><p> </p><p> </p><p> </p></div></div>
2985	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Criminal Law Amendment Act, 1958</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Citation:</b>  6 MLR (2002) (HC) 162, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 213,7 MLR (2002) (HC) 265. 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 323.. </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>
