inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 5 and 14— Cancellation of bail on ground of abuse of the privilege of bail—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Bail in a non-bailable case is a concession to the accused in trust. Such bail can be cancelled if the accused abuses the privilege of bail. <em>Tayazuddin and another Vs. the State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 20.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995— Section 6(1)— offence of rape—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Children Act, 1974—Trial of Juvenile offender—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the offender is a child below 16 years of age he has to be tried under the Children Act, 1974. Court is under a duty in such situation to undertake enquiry to ascertain the age of the accused, otherwise the trial of a child under the common law will be without jurisdiction rendering the conviction and sentence a nullity. <em>Monir Hossain (Md.) Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 275.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995 (Act No. XVIII of 1995)—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 6(1)- Minimum punishment for offence of rape can not be reduced in appeal —</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Accused can well be convicted for the offence of rape on the basis of solitary evidence of the victim when her evidence appears in all probabilities to be reliable and trustworthy. There is no imperative of the law that the court shall always look for independent corroboration in rape case. Since the minimum punishment for rape is imprisonment for life as provided under section 6(1) of the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Ain 1995, there is no scope to reduce the sentence in appeal under section 423 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898.<em>Manirid Islam (Md.) Vs. The State, <span style="mso-font-width: 66%;">8 </span>MLR (2003) (HC) 27.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Sidhan) Ain, 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 6(1) and 8(2)— Offence of ape and engaging women for moral purposes—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 20— Appeal against ejection of bail— Grant of bail when here is no allegation of overt act against the accused—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Where in a case there is no specific negations of any overt act on the part f the accused made in the F.I.R. and here is no specific incriminating laterals shown in the charge-sheet gainst the accused, he may be granted ail in case of such nature. <em>Abu Taker Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) HC) 308.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjaton (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 6(1) and 14— Offence of rape- proof of charge- withholding material witness- inordinate delay in ) lodging F.I.R. all taken together lakes the prosecution case untrustworthy—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In order to secure conviction prosecution has to prove the charge ith cogent and consistent evidence beyond all reasonable doubt. The inordinate delay in lodging F.I.R without satisfactory explanation, non-production of alamat and withholding ital witness from being examined render the prosecution case unworthy of credence. <em>Hossain Shially (Fakir) Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 355.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Narl-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishes Bidhan) Ain 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Section 6(2)- Death is proper punishment for rape and murder</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">-When the charge of commission of rape and murder of victim girl is proved beyond doubt, death is the appropriate punishment. <em>Azad Mia alias Md. Azad Vs. The State,7 MLR (2002) (AD) 22.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 6(2)— Offence of rape and murder and the proper sentence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the charge of rape and murder is established by circumstantial evidence supported by consistent witness the accused can safely be convicted and the proper sentence is the death sentence. Prosecution is not required to produce each and every witness during trial. Reasonable doubt depends on degree of doubt.<em>State Vs. Awal Fakir (Md.). 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 297.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 6(3)— Offence of rape and punishment—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Confessional statement recorded under section 164, Cr.P.C. when found true and voluntary can form the sole basis of conviction against the confessing accused. It is not binding upon other co-accused but such confessional statement when corroborated by independent evidence can also form the basis of conviction of other non-confessing accused.<em>Nuruddin alias Shahabuddin and another Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 379.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 6(4)— For the offence of rape and murder, the proper sentence is death—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In case of custodial death the custodian has to explain the circumstances under which the victim died—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When it is established that the victim was taken to the custody of the accused in the dead hours of the night and in the following morning her dead body was found with injuries on throat and her private parts with sign of rape and the explanation offered being not satisfactory the sentence of death has been held by the apex court as perfectly justified. <em>Mainiri Haque and another Vs. The State., 9 MLR (2004) (AD) 321.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 9(c)— offence of abduction for committing rape—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Delay in lodging F.I.R when satisfactorily explained is not fatal. Even when the charge of rape is not proved, conviction can well be based on evidence of the victim girl when found reliable and inspires confidence for the offence of abduction. <em>Misti </em>and <em>others Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 394.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishes Bidhan) Ain 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 9(ka)- Offence of immoral act punishable under section 9(G)—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Taking nude photographs of victims by force for the purpose of black mailing is highly immoral act.—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">When major charge of rape fails accused may be punished for minor offence of immoral act. No observation on extraneous matter not relevant to the merit of the case should be made in the Judgment against outsider</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">In a case charge of rape when fails, the accused who took nude photographs of the victim by force may well be punished under section </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">9(G) <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">of the </span>1995 <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">Ain when such a highly immoral act Is proved beyond doubt though no charge was framed therefore. Since the accused were fully aware of the details of the occurrence and cross examined the prosecution witnesses on this point, such conviction is perfectly maintainable as no prejudice was caused to the accused.</span><em>Rajib Kamrul Hassan and three others Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 70.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;"> </span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Section 10(1) and 14</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">Causing death of wife for dowry— Offence triable by Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Adalat. When death of wife caused not for dowry offence is triable by the Sessions Judge—</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">News paper report not admissible in evidence</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">When the death of a wife is caused for dowry, the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Adalat is vested with jurisdiction to try such offence. Otherwise the offence of murder is triable by the Session Judge.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">News paper report is not admissible in evidence without the reporter being examined on oath.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">When evidence on record materially contradict with regard to the manner of occurence and cause of death of the victim, conviction and sentence passed thereon cannot be sustainable. </span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Osena Begum and another Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 57.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Section 10(1)</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">Offence of causing death of wife for dowry— Conviction and sentence can be based on circumstantial evidence—</span></span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Circumstantial evidence can form the basis of conviction when the same unerringly points at the guilt of the accused. </span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The State Vs. Nasiruddin (Nasiruddin Vs. State), 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 82.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">Section 10(1)</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">Punishment for causing death of wife for dowry—</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Charge can well be proved by circumstantial evidence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There is no imperative of the law that every commission of offence should be proved by direct ocular evidence. When the husband fails to offer any satisfactory explanation as to how his wife was murdered, when they were living in the same house at the time of the occurence, the husband accused can well be convicted on the basis of circumstantial evidence.<em>State Vs. Md. Kaloo, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 101</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishes Bidhan) Ain, 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 12— Offence of child trafficking and the penalty—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Evidence Act, 1872—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 118— Evidence of child witness is admissible—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The cardinal principle of criminal jurisprudence is that the prosecution must prove the charge against the accused with consistent and reliable evidence beyond all reasonable doubt. When material evidence are withheld and the evidence brought on record are inconsistent and the charge does not stand proved to the hilt beyond all reasonable doubt the accused is entitled to be acquitted on benefit of doubt. Such doubt must not be imaginary or fanciful. <em>State Vs. Abul Kashem, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 164.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Nirjatan Daman Ain, 2000— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 19— Restrictions on granting bail to accused—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Section 25— Powers of Sessions Judge or High Court Division to grant bail-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Powers<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Tribunal<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>or the Sessions Judge or the High Court Division are restricted under section <span style="mso-font-width: 60%;">19<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span>of the Ain and bail to the accused cannot be granted except on the grounds enumerated there under. <em>Shahid Malongi (Md.) and another Vs.The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 173.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 24— Provides for appeal against conviction and sentence within 30 days.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When provisions of appeal under the special law with special limitation are available application under section 561A Cr.P.C. for quashment of conviction and sentence does not lie. <em>Sharifa Begum @ Sharu Bibi Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 239.</em></span></p></div></div>
2996	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 2000</h2>

Roman','serif';">Section 9(1)— Offence of rape and punishment—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 22— Recording statement of the victim or witness</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">As provided under section 22 of the Ain of 2000 statement of victim or <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">a </span>witness shall be recorded under section 22 of the Ain and not under section 164 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. Statement recorded under section 164 Cr.P.C. in case under the Ain shall be treated as one recorded under section 22 of the Ain of 2000.<em>Wasim Mia (Md.) and another Vs. <span style="letter-spacing: 1.0pt;">The </span>State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 162.</em></span><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml> <o:OfficeDocumentSettings>  <o:RelyOnVML/>  <o:AllowPNG/> </o:OfficeDocumentSettings></xml><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Ain, 2000—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 11(ka)— Penalty for causing death for dowry—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The settled principle of law is that in a wife killing case when it is established that both the husband and the victim wife were residing in the same house at the relevant time, the husband is under the obligation to explain the circumstances under which his wife died.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the charge is proved beyond all reasonable doubt the sentence of death is held to be perfectly justified.<em>State Vs. Md. Ainul Haqne. 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 393.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 9.1pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span table.MsoNormalTable	{mso-style-name:"Table Normal";	mso-tstyle-rowband-size:0;	mso-tstyle-colband-size:0;	mso-style-noshow:yes;	mso-style-priority:99;	mso-style-qformat:yes;	mso-style-parent:"";	mso-padding-alt:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Calibri","sans-serif";	mso-ascii-font-family:Calibri;	mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;}</style><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">                                                        Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138 and 141— Complaint to be lodged within the specified period—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Cheque can be presented to the Bank for payment within 6(six) months from the date of issue. Complaint shall have to be lodged within one month of the date of the cause of action arising from the failure of the drawer of the cheque incompliance with the notice issued by the drawee within 15(fifteen) days after the cheque was returned being dishonored. When the complaint does not satisfy the above requirements and does not disclose cause of action, the proceeding is quashed being abuse of the process of the court. <em>Nizamuddin Mahmood Vs. Abdul Hatnid Bhiriyan and another, 9 MLR (2004) (AD) 299.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138— Case against offence for issuing<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>cheque which is dishonored has to be filed within statutory period—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The case initiating criminal proceeding shall be filed within the statutory period prescribed therefore. Where no steps are taken within the time specified under section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881, the cause of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>action<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>unlike<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>in other </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">situation for prosecution goes by default or the right accruing there under is barred by limitation. This special remedy can be availed of only when steps are taken within prescribed time.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Otherwise the criminal proceedings being not sustainable in law are liable to be quashed. In such a case alternative remedy is available in civil court.</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Abdus <em>Salam Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 270.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> </span></p></div></div>

class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">                                                Payment of Wages Act, </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">1936 </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"><span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">Section </span>20<span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">— Chief Accounts Officer not being a worker, Labour court has no jurisdiction to interfere with his dismissal from service—</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">The Chief Accounts Officer of Daily Janata News Papers is not a worker within the meaning a section 1(b) of the Payment of Wages Act, 1936 as his duties are of administrative and supervisory nature and as such the Labour Court has no jurisdiction under section 20 of the Act to interfere with his dismissal from service. Accordingly the conviction and sentence passed by the Labour Court</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">are set aside. Sanaullah Noori' (M.) <em>Editor Dainik Janata Vs.</em> Chairman 3rd <em>Labour Court, Dhaka and others, </em>6 MLR <em>(2001)(HC) </em>305.</span></p></div></div>
2999	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Penal Code, 1860</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Citation:</b>  8 MLR (2003) (HC) 409, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 91, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 135,10 MLR (2005) (HC) 91, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 208, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 11, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 114, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 17,10 MLR (2005) (HC) 108, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 70, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 100, 6 ML</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  1860</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Criminal Law</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2018-03-25</p><!DOCTYPE html><p><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml> <o:OfficeDocumentSettings>  <o:RelyOnVML/>  <o:AllowPNG/> </o:OfficeDocumentSettings></xml><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">                                                                       Penal Code, 1860 </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 34- Joint liability—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Joint liability of the accused for offence committed in furtherance of common intention. Participation in the commission of the offence is the essence of such common intention. <em>Khokon Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 409.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">Code, </span>1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 34— Joint liability— active participation necessary—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 34 of the Penal Code, 1860 lays down the principle of joint liability in respect of commission of crime which presupposes existence of common intention and preplan. When crime is committed in furtherance of common intention each and every such person having taken active part in the commission of crime shall be equally liable to the same punishment.<em>State Vs. Mir Hossain and others, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 91.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">Code, </span>1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 34- <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">Common </span>intention in <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">the </span>commission <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">of murder and </span>joint Accused</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">-</span></p><p class="Style4" style="line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Common intention as defined in section <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">34r</span> of the Penal Code, 1860 implies acting in concert with preplan. The intention becomes common</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> intention of all the accused persons when the intention of one accused is shared by other accused and all such accused are equally liable for the offence when done in furtherance of common intention. The essence of section 34 is participation in action. <em>The State Vs. Ershad AH Sikdar and others, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 135.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 34— Joint liability— active participation necessary— Evidentiary value of confessional statement.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Law is well settled that crime need not be always proved by direct ocular evidence. Circumstantial evidence may well form the basis of conviction. Accused can well be convicted on the basis of his confessional statement when found true and voluntary. Confessional statement of an accused cannot be used against other co-accused unless such confessional statement is corroborated by other independent evidence. Circumstantial evidence may also be considered as corroborative evidence.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 34 of the Penal Code, 1860 lays down the principle of joint liability in respect of commission of crime which presupposes existence of common intention and preplan. When crime is committed in furtherance of common intention each and every such person having taken active part in the commission of crime shall be equally liable to the same punishment. <em>State Vs. Mir Hossain and others, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 91.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.25pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 53— Forfeiture is one kind of punishment— Confiscation is not penalty but one of the modes for disposal of property in trial.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.25pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The term forfeiture is distinguishable from confiscation. Forfeiture is one kind of penalty while confiscation is not a penalty as defined under section 53.<em>Mobarakullah (Md.) and another Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 208.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 68 and 69</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <strong>Payment of fine in installments—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">As there is express provision contained in sections 68 and 69 of the Penal Code for payment of fine and termination of sentence following thereof, the Appellate Division rejected the prayer for payment of fine in installments in exercise of the power under article 104 of the Constitution. <em>Lt. General (Retd.) H.M. Ershad Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 11.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case where from the facts and circumstances and materials on record a case of right of private defence is made out, the plea of self defence is available to the accused. The court can well take this into consideration even though such defence is not specifically pleaded or half heartedly pleaded. <em>RukhuMia Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 114.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 100</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <strong>Exercise of self-defence in causing death of aggressor—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Right of self defence can be exercised to the extent of causing death of the assailant/aggressor within the limitations as provided under section 99 of the Penal Code. When the wife inflicted injury on the male organ of the husband when he was asleep and found inflicting further injuries on his person in vital part when he woke up, the husband has been found justified in inflicting injury to his wife causing her death in exercise of right of self defence under section 100 of the Penal Code and is thus acquitted of the charge under section 302 of the Penal Code. <em>Hasan Rony Vs. the State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 17.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 107 and 109</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <strong>Abetment of commission of offence—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Unless the ingredients as enumerated under section 107 of <span style="mso-font-width: 60%;">the </span>Penal Code are found present <span style="mso-font-width: 60%;">there </span>cannot be an offence of abetment punishable under section 109 of <span style="mso-font-width: 60%;">the </span>Code. Mere request to do something does not constitute offence of abetment and as such proceedings drawn there for being the abuse of the process of court is liable to be quashed. <em>Abdur Rahman Dhali and others Vs. Tk State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 108.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 109</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <strong>Offence of abetment-Section 201- Principal accused cannot be punished under section 201.</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Offence of abetment is a separate and distinct offence and is punishable with the same punishment as prescribed <span style="mso-font-width: 60%;">for </span>the principal offence abetted. <span style="mso-font-width: 60%;">When </span>the principal charge fails conviction can not be awarded for abetment. <em>Khokon Mridha and another Vs. Tk State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 70.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 148 and 302/114—Offence o rioting and murder—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Benefit of doubt cannot be claim as a matter <span style="letter-spacing: -1.0pt;">of</span> right—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Doubt as to the complicity of the accused has to be established in the light of the evidence on record in <span style="letter-spacing: -1.0pt;">re</span>mind of the judge.That certain accused is given the benefit of doubt can not be the ground for claiming the same treatment by the other accused who stands on different footing. When charge against the convict-petitioner stands proved beyond all reasonable doubt he can not claim acquittal on benefit of doubt. <em>Moazzem Hossain Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 100.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code 1860— Section 149—Common object and constructive liability</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When five or more persons being armed with deadly weapons and forming an unlawful assembly encircled the deceased and variously assaulted him who as a result died, each and every such accused is equally guilty of the charge of murder under section 302 committed, in furtherance of their common object as contemplated under section 149 of the Penal Code. <em>Ishacjue Peada (Mridha) (Md.) Vs. The <span style="mso-font-width: 75%;">State, </span>6 MLR (2001) (AD) 296.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, I860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302- Altering the charge into one under section 304 part 1 and reducing the sentence to 10 years R.I</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case of murder where the convict-petitioner was sentenced to imprisonment for life by the trial court which has been reduced to 10 years R.I. upon altering the charge into one under section 304 part I by the High Court Division in appeal in view of the mitigating circumstance, the occurrence taking place in a bid to resist the taking away of pulse grown by the convict- petitioner, there being no illegality committed in the impugned judgment and order warranting any interference leave to appeal is refused. <em>Emdadul Haque Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 98.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302/34— Conviction and sentence when based on consistent evidence calls for no interference</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Where the conviction and sentence are based on concurrent findings of the trial court and the High Court Division upon proper appreciation of evidence and when no legal infirmity could be pointed out, the leave petition is rejected. <em>Abu Jamal &amp; another Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 29.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302/34 and 396— Nature of proof—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The well established principle of law is that in order to secure conviction the prosecution must prove the charge against the accused by consistent and reliable evidence. When there is no legal and reliable evidence on record as to the proof of charge beyond doubt accused cannot be convicted on any other hypothesis. <em>The State Vs. Azim Sarder and another, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 103.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Charge of murder-Nature of proof</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">-Contradictions on material points by eye witnesses make the prosecution case doubtful-Contradictions in the evidence of the eye witnesses on material points as to the manner of occurrence make the prosecution case doubtful. When the decision and findings of the High Court Division do not suffer from any misreading of the evidence, the impugned judgment and order of reversal of conviction and sentence does not call for any interference. The State<em> Vs. Nasir Ahmed @ Nastruddin and another, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 194.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Charge of murder-Legal requirement as to proof of— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Evidence Act, 1872— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 3 and 30— Evidentiary value of confessional statement</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The well settled principle of law is that the confessional statement of one accused cannot be used against the other co-accused. Moreover the confessional statement recorded under section 30 is not an evidence within the meaning of section 3 of the Evidence Act, 1872. When none of the eyewitnesses of the occurrence said a single word against the convict-appellant, this is factually a case of no evidence. Therefore the impugned order of conviction and sentence which is not based on any legal evidence is set aside with a serious stricture against the learned trial Court judge.<em>Abu Syed Vs.The State, </em>6 <em>MLR (2001) (HC) 237.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Charge of murder—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Onus of proof lies upon the prosecution</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">No hard and fast rule as to number of witness to be examined- Partisan witness need not always be discarded—The cardinal principle of criminal jurisprudence is that the onus entirely lies upon the prosecution to prove the charge against the accused to the hilt beyond all reasonable doubt. There is no hard and fast rule as to the number of witness the prosecution has to examine. In a case where there are huge number of witnesses, the prosecution is not required to examine each and every of them. It is enough to secure conviction if the material witnesses are examined. Partisan witnesses where in the circumstances are probable and reliable can not be discarded merely on the ground of their being partisan. Suffering the pangs of death for long time pending disposal of reference and appeal are considered to be good ground for altering the sentence of death into one of imprisonment for life. <em>The State Vs. Md. MonirAhmed @ MomrHossain, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 243.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302- Motive as to murder is not always necessary to be proved—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When there are sufficient reliable evidence establishing the charge beyond doubt, motive for the murder need not be proved. Inquest report being the part of investigation alongside the post mortem report can well be used by the court as to the condition of the dead body. <em>Anisur Rahman Chowdhwy Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (AD) 119.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, I860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302- Motive when to be proved—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In murder trial motive is not always essential and need not be proved by the prosecution. But when motive is alleged then the prosecution has to prove it.Salim <em>(Md.) Vs. The State, </em>7 <em>MLR (2002) (HC) 20.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <strong>Murder of wife by husband- Circumstantial evidence—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When wife is murdered in the house of the husband while living together with the husband, the husband has the liability to explain under what circumstances his wife died. When ocular evidence is hardly possible from the neighbors or inmates of the house circumstantial evidence can well form the basis of conviction against the husband-accused. Reasonable doubt has to be adjudged commensurate to the nature of the offence. <em>Alfazuddin Khan (Md.) Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 73.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <strong>Charge of murder— Section 84- Acquittal on ground of insanity-</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Defence of insanity if taken shall have to be proved by the defence. Legal insanity when proved can be the ground for acquittal of the accused. Criminal Lunatic may be detained in asylum till cure. <em>Nikhil Chandra Haider Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 115.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Charge of murder—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Evidence Act, 1872—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 32— Dying declaration-Evidentiary value for conviction</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Dying declaration has a special sanctity in view of the fact that a dying man as expected cannot tell lie and as such a dying declaration when considered true can alone form the basis of conviction.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Order of acquittal which is perverse and is based on findings on improper appreciation of evidence need be set aside. The High Court Division in such a case is required to interfere with the order of acquittal which is shockingly unconscionable. <em>The State Vs. Rashid Ahmed and others, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 147.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Charge of murder— Acquittal of accused on proof of alibi— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Evidence Act, 1872— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 11— Acquittal on proof of Alibi</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">-When satisfactorily established by evidence such as attendance Register that the accused was on duty in his office at the relevant time of the occurrence,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>accused<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>may be acquitted on such plea of alibi. <em>Nurid Islam Vs. Abdul Malek and another, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 37.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Murder charge in a wife killing case— Husband's liability</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Husband is liable to explain as to how his wife died when both of them were residing in the same house. When the explanation as to cause of death being suicidal is proved false by medical evidence, the husband in the face of the evidence and circumstance can well be held guilty of the charge of murder. <em>Abul Hossain Khan Vs. The State, <span style="mso-font-width: 75%;">8 </span>MLR (2003) (AD) 191.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Sentence of death commuted on ground of young age and suffering the pangs of death for long period</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Commutation of sentence of death into imprisonment for life by High Court Division held perfectly justified by the apex court on consideration of age of the convict appellant, his inflicting only one injury and his being in the condemned cell for 3(three) years. <em>Shamim (Md.) alias Shamim Sikder Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 214.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Sentence of death is justified when death is caused with extreme brutality—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Motive of murder— Motive when taken has to be proved</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case of murder motive is not always required to be proved. When there is ocular evidence of the occurrence motive is immaterial. That injuries-were not caused in the vital parts of the body and the victim died after 7 days of the occurrence is no mitigating factor for awarding lesser penalty. When injuries are caused on the less vital parts of the body with a view to prolonging the pains of death, the sentence of death has been held in such a case by the apex court to be perfectly justified. <em>Ershad All Sikder (Md.) Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (AD) 355.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302/34— Charge of murder-proof by circumstantial evidence</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sentence for 30 years is not authorized- Imprisonment for life is the proper term of sentence—When chain of events are proved by consistent witness and the calling of the deceased by the accused and the trail of marks of blood found from the P.O. house to the place where the dead body was detected constitute most strong circumstantial evidence irresistibly leading to the conclusion as to the guilt of the accused beyond all reasonable doubt. <em>Bhola Vs. The State, 7 </em>MLR(2002)(HC) 224.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 6.5pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Penal Code, 1860— (Act XLV of I860)—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Conviction on the basis of circumstantial evidence in a wife killing case is permissible when the husband fails to satisfactorily explain his conduct—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Where in a case of murder of a wife it is established that at the time of occurrence both the deceased wife and husband were in the same house, the husband is bound to explain the circumstance Linder which his wife died. In the absence of satisfactory explanation the husband can well be convicted for the charge of murder of his wife on the basis of circumstantial evidence pointing at the guilt of the accused to the excisions of any other hypothesis. <em>Giasuddin Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 21.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302- Charge of murder can be reduced to that under section 304 when there is no premeditation</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In the absence of premeditation, the killing of wife by husband following altercation falls to the category of culpable homicide not amounting to murder and charge can be reduced to one under section 304 of the Penal Code. Principal accused cannot be convicted for charge both under section 302 and 201 of the Penal Code. <em>Manu Mia Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 66.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— Section 302 and 34— Charge of murder— Nature of proof</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In order to secure conviction and sentence in criminal case particularly in murder trial the prosecution has to prove the charges against accused beyond all reasonable doubt. Non-production of alamat such as the torch being the only means of recognition of the accused, Sketch map of the P.O. and non-examination of the Investigating officer including material C.S. witnesses without explanation render the prosecution case doubtful and as such the conviction and sentence based on discrepant evidence are held not sustainable in law. <em>Mokbul Hossain and another Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 67.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><strong>Penal Code, 1860— </strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 15.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><strong>Section 302</strong>—Charge of murder-Sentence of death commuted on ground of absence of ocular evidence and suffering the pangs of death for more than two years—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the victim wife was found with her husband last and thereafter dead body with injuries was recovered on the following day, the husband is under the obligation to explain the circumstance under which his wife died. Strong circumstantial evidence pointing unerringly at the guilt of the accused to the exclusion of any other hypothesis, can safely form the basis of conviction.
