Since the convict appellant suffered the pangs of death for long, the sentence is commuted into imprisonment for life. <em>State Vs.Abdur Rahim. </em>9 MLR (2004) (HC) 309.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— Section<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>302—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Punishment for murder—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 34— Common intention in the commission of offence with active participation</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— When evidence are contradictory and discrepant— Conviction thereon not sustainable-Sentence of either death or imprisonment for life in order to be sustainable must be based on consistent and reliable evidence. When evidence are discrepant, sharply contradictory and suffer from legal infirmity can not form the basis of conviction. In the absence of pre-plan and active participation in the commission of the offence section 34 of the Penal Code is not attracted. <em>Deviz and others Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 344.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Punishment for murder</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 1.9pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Normally in a case of murder death is the appropriate sentence. Alternative sentence of imprisonment for life may be awarded when there are mitigating circumstances such as in the instant case altercation between the convict and the deceased and the age of the convict being at the prime of 25 years. In that view the sentence of death is commuted into imprisonment for life. <em>State Vs. Adam Khan 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 405.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Husband's liability in a wife killing case</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Husband has the liability to explain the circumstance under which his wife died when both of them were residing in the same house at the time of the occurrence. When the explanation offered is found false and the wife is found to have died due to injuries Penal Code, 1860<strong>—</strong> which were ante-mortem and homicidal in nature the conviction and sentence of the husband is held to have been perfectly justified in the face of the attending circumstances. <em>Sheik Moksed Ali Vs. The State, </em><span style="letter-spacing: 1.0pt;">20 MLR </span><em>(2005) (AD) 27.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .95pt 0in .0001pt 11.05pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302 and 201— Circumstantial evidence can well form the basis of conviction and sentence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Motive— Prosecution is not always required to prove the motive of murder</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Circumstantial evidence unerringly pointing at the guilt of the accused and when the same is incapable of any other hypothesis other than the guilt of the accused can safely form the basis of conviction and sentence.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Court has to conclusively decide the guilt or otherwise of the accused in clear terms but cannot leave the accused to be punished by Allah. This is peculiar and unknown method which the apex court strongly disapproved and upon reassessment of the evidence on record convicted accused respondent since acquitted by the High Court Division.<em>State Vs. Khondker Zillul Bari and others, 10 MLR (2005) (AD) 175.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302/34— Causing death of a person without common intention does not attract Section 304— Culpable homicide not amounting to murder</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Wife's liability in a husband killing case—It is well settled that in a wife killing case husband owes an obligation to explain the circumstance under which his wife died when they were residing in the same house at the time of the occurrence. Similarly in a case of murder of the husband the wife has also a liability to explain the circumstance under which her husband was killed when they were residing in the same house at the time of the occurrence. In the absence of common intention of committing the murder, section 34 of the Penal Code is not attracted. Again when the ingredient of the culpable homicide amounting to murder is absent, the offence is punishable under section 304 of the Penal Code. Extra judicial confession when found true and voluntary can form the basis of conviction. <em>State Vs. Jahanara Begum and another. 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 11.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Charge of murder to be proved beyond all reasonable doubt</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Since the charge of murder involves capital punishment, the proof in support thereof must be based on consistent and reliable evidence. When the identity of the dead body is not established, the evidence are inconsistent and are not worthy of credence, the conviction and sentence passed thereon cannot be sustainable in the eye of law. <em>Nazir Hossain alias Chhota Kachua Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 169.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Husband can not be saddled with the liability of murdering his wife when it is established that he was not present in the p.o. house at the time of occurrence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It is well settled that the husband has to explain as to how his wife was killed when the wife was living with the husband in the p.o. house at the relevant time. But when it is established that he was not in the p.o. house at the material time the husband can not be saddled with the liability of killing his wife and in that view of the matter the convict-appellant in the instant case is acquitted .<em>Abu Taher Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 282.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.95pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.95pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 154— Delay in lodging F.I.R— Legal consequence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Charge of murder— proof beyond all reasonable doubt</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sustainability of conviction and sentence when evidence are contradictory and suffer from improbability— Non-appealing convict may be allowed the benefit of acquittal passed in appeal preferred by co-convicts—When not satisfactorily explained the inordinate delay in lodging FIR is fatal to the prosecution which casts adverse reflection on the prosecution as to concoction and embellishment. To secure sustainability of conviction and sentence the same must be based on consistent and reliable evidence. The burden of proof entirely lies upon the prosecution to prove the charge beyond shadow of all reasonable doubt. When the evidence of the ocular witness are sharply contradictory and suffer from legal infirmity and fall far below the level of credence the conviction and sentence passed thereon cannot be sustained in the eye of law. It has now become ccepted principle that the benefit of lie judgment of acquittal can be extended to non-appealing convicts. <em>Kalam Tahikder and others Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 264.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"> </p><p class="Style7" style="line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="Style7" style="line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Sentence of death is the proper sentence in a case of brutal murder in the absence of any mitigating factor— Confessional statement true and voluntary can form the basis of conviction—</span></strong></p><p class="Style7" style="line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It is not necessary that commission of offence must always be proved by ocular evidence. Circumstantial evidence unerringly pointing at the guilt of the accused can well form the sole basis of conviction. Confessional statement of accused recorded under section 164 Cr.P.C. when found voluntary and true can well be the basis of conviction.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="Style7" style="line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case of brutal murder sentence of death is the proper punishment which should be awarded unless there is any mitigating factor.<em>Kalu Mia Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 397.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Charge of murder and the proof thereof—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Charge need not always be proved by ocular evidence. Circumstantial evidence unerringly pointing at the guilt of the accused can well form the basis of conviction. Husband has heavy liability to explain the circumstance under which his wife was murdered when they were living in the same house at the time of the occurrence. In the absence of any satisfactory explanation from the husband, the medical evidence together with the absconsion of the accused immediately after the occurrence and the chain of other attending circumstance unerringly pointing at the guilt of the convict-accused the learned judges of the High Court Division having found the conviction and sentence perfectly justified confirmed the sentence of death. <em>State Vs. Md. Delwar Hossain Faraji condemned prisoner, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 375.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302— Sentence for charge of murder may be either death or imprisonment for life—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 34 and 109— Common intention and abetment operate in two different situation—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 237 Cr.P.C— Punishment may be imposed for different offence when proved though not charged there for—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When charge of murder committed with brutality is established the death penalty is appropriate. Where in a case mitigating circumstance exists alternative sentence of imprisonment for life would be the proper sentence.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 34 is attracted when the accused in furtherance of their common intention commit the murder. In case of section 34 participation in commission of offence is the constituent ingredient while section 109 is attracted where conspiracy and abetment in the commission of offence is done.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Accused may be convicted for the offence proved as provided under section 237Cr.P.C. even though the charge was not framed therefore. <em>Ershad AH Sikdar and others Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 192.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 304 Part-1— offence of culpable homicide not amounting to murder—Legal effect of non-examination of the I.O.—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Intention to cause bodily injuries likely to cause death may be gathered from the nature of weapon used and the manner of inflicting injuries. The Court, has to give its finding while fixing the offence under section 304 part-1 of the Penal Code. When the offence is proved with consistent evidence of ocular witness and the accused is not prejudiced the non-examination of the investigating officer is not fatal for the prosecution. <em>Nasir Howlader Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 99. </em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 304</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">— <strong>Culpable homicide not amounting to murder</strong>— </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Procedure of sentencing in case of the accused being in long custody—In the absence of common intention to cause death it is culpable homicide not amounting to murder punishable under section 304 of the Penal Code.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">The custody of the accused for long time pending trial or hearing of appeal may be taken into account and deducted from the total sentence to be awarded.State Vs. <em>Abdul Barek and others, 7 MLR (2002) (AD) 17.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 304</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">— <strong>Alteration of charge under section 302</strong>— <strong>Where mitigating circumstances are present</strong>—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">When the victim died as a result of injury inflicted upon his person by the accused in occurrence arising out of quarrel offering sudden provocation, the appropriate charge will be under section 304 part II of Penal Code for the offence of culpable homicide not amounting to murder. Accordingly the charge u/s 302 is altered and the sentence is reduced. <em>Nabir Chandra Chowdhury and others Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 256.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 304</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">— <strong>Charge of culpable homicide has to be established by cogent and acceptable legal evidence— No moral conviction is sustainable—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Conviction must be based on cogent and acceptable legal evidence. There is no room in criminal jurisprudence for moral conviction. <em>Habez Md. Peru Kazi Vs. The Stale, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) </em>333</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> <br/></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 304 Parte II, 342, 448/149— Charge of culpable homicide not amounting to murder</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">The cardinal principle of criminal justice is that the charge against the accused must be proved beyond shadow of all reasonable doubt in order to secure conviction.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Though it is permissible in law that an accused may be convicted on the basis of evidence of solitary witness the rule of produce demands corroboration thereof by independent witness when there is admitted existence of enmity between the parties. Non-examination of neutral witness casts adverse reflection on the credibility of the prosecution case which took place in a free fight between rival groups of hundreds of people.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The guilt or innocence of accused must be ascertained on the assessment of the totality of evidence and no such conclusion should be drawn on the basis of isolated scrutiny of evidence. <em>Niirul Islam and others Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 416.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 324— Piece of stone when used to cause injury is weapon of offence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Piece of stone when used to cause injury on vital part of body is a weapon of offence. Prosecution has to prove the charge. Defense has no obligation. <em>Mashuq Mia © Iqbal Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (AD) 372.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 326A- Grievous hurt caused by acid throwing or corrosive substance</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- Punishment therefore-Causing grievous hurt such as disfiguring face and body permanently by throwing acid or corrosive substance is heinous offence not only against the victim but also against humanity. Punishment for such offence must be deterrent, otherwise legislative intent would be frustrated. <em>Dulal Modhu Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 53</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 21— Public Servant— Section 332— DESA Employee is Public Servant—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Victim Abdul Malek an employee of DESA is a public servant within the meaning of section 21 clause 12(b) of the Penal Code and as such the charge under section 332 of the Penal Code has been perfectly justified warranting no interference. <em>Taleb Hossain @ Abu Taleb Hossaln Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 219.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 363— Offence of Kidnapping— Consent of minor is immaterial—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When it is proved by consistent evidence that the minor victim girl was kidnapped by enticement, the conviction and sentence awarded upon the accused are perfectly justified. The consent of the minor is immaterial and is of no legal consequence. <em>Abdul Karim Vs. The Stale, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 341</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> <br/></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 364— Husband's liability in wife missing case is the same as in the case of wife killing</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The husband is under the obligation to explain satisfactorily the circumstances under which his wife is missing when at the relevant time she was living with him in the same house. The same principle of the wife killing case as to the husband's liability is similarly applicable to a wife missing case. <em>Abdul Majid Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC)313.<br/></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 376— Charge of rape—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Evidence of the victim even though not corroborated by eye witness can form the sole basis of conviction—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case of rape there can hardly be any eye witness of the occurrence. When the evidence of the victim woman appears to be reliable in the absence of any proof of enmity and no inconsistency thereof transpired, such evidence of the victim alone may form the basis of conviction. When the conviction and sentence of the convict-petitioner are based on the concurrent findings of the trial court as well of the High Court Division and when such findings do not suffer from any legal infirmity, no interference is called for. <em>Abu Taker Mia alias Taker Mia Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (AD) 77.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, I860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 376- Punishment for offence of rape—Alteration of conviction and sentence from section 4(c) of the Ordinance 1983 to section 376 of the Penal Code—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case which was tried by the Special Tribunal and the accused was convicted and sentenced for offence of rape and when subsequently it was found that the offence should have been tried by the Session Judge where the same person presiding over both the Session Court and Tribunal, the conviction and sentence has been altered from section 4(c) of the Ordinance, 1983 into one under section 376 of the Penal Code having regard to the legislative intent and purpose instead allowing the ends of justice frustrated by technicalities.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It is further held by the High Court Division that conviction and sentence can well be based on the solitary evidence of the prosecutrix if it inspires the confidence of the Court. Section 134 of the Evidence Act, 1872 does not provide for any particular number of witness to prove any particular charge, the golden rule of evidence being that evidence has to be weighed but not counted. <em>Shibu Pada Acharjee Vs. The State, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 275.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 376- Offence of rape-Evidentiary value of the prosecutrix-when corroboration is required</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- In a case of rape where the prosecutrix is the sole witness of the occurrence, in the absence of surrounding circumstances, her evidence must be scrutinized closely and corroboration by independent witness becomes necessary. The absence of mark of violance in the person of the victim makes the prosecution case doubtful. <em>Masad Mia (Md.) Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 28.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 382— Commission of theft is pre-requisite of an offence— Non-appealing convict may be allowed the benefit of acquittal</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Unless there is a case of theft with preparation to cause death or hurt to escape, section 382 of the Penal Code is not attracted. When the prosecution case is found wholly not proved, the non-appealing convict may also be given the benefit of acquittal. <em>Mafizid Islam Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 108.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— Section 395 and 397- Conviction to be based on legal evidence</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When prosecution fails to bring home the charge under section 395 and 397 of the Penal Code by any cogent evidence<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>as<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>to<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>identity and participation of the accused in the commission of the offence, no conviction can be passed on basis of surmise or any other hypothesis. <em>Belal alias Belial and 2 others Vs. the State, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 27.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.95pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.95pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 395 and 397— Offence of dacoity</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— When enmity between the parties from before the occurrence exists, corroboration of partisan witness by independent witness is necessary— Although there is no rule of law requiring corroboration by independent witness, the rule of prudence demands corroboration of partisan witness by independent witness particularly when enmity between the parties exists from before the occurrence. <em>Mahmudul Huq and others Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 105.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860— Section 396— Charge of dacoity with murder- Nature of proof—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Confessional statement of one accused cannot form the sole basis of conviction against other co accused without independent corroborative evidence. Therefore, the conviction based on such confessional statement</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> alone is not sustainable in the eye of law. <em>The State Vs. Md.Tuku Biswas, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 33.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860— Section 399- Offence of preparation to commit dacoity-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Though there is express provision for offence of preparation to commit dacoity, there is no provision in the Penal Code as to offence of preparation by persons below 5 in number to commit robbery. The Penal Code has been suggested to be amended to this direction. <em>KaramAli Vs. the State, </em>7 <em>MLR (2002) (HC) 79.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">— <strong>406 and 420</strong>— <strong>Loan money does not constitute offence—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 561A</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">— <strong>Quashment of proceedings-to prevent the abuse of the process of court—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Unless there is inducement and entrustment loan taken for business purpose and failure or refusal to repay the same is a civil liability and does not constitute offence punishable under section 406 and 420 of the Penal Code. Therefore the proceedings being abuse of the process of Court are quashed. <em>Abdul Mannan Sarker (Md.) Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC). 279.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 406</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">— <strong>Dishonest misappro­priation—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">When the convict appellant took the shallow machine from the Krishi Bank against loan but subsequently sold away the same without permission of the Bank and adjustment of outstanding dues in violation of the pledge, this amounts to dishonest misappropriation and breach of trust punishable under section 406 of the Penal Code, 1860. <em>Kalimidlah Topadar (Md) Vs. The State and another, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 39.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> <br/></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 406/420— Where the initial intention of cheating is absent, prosecution under section 420 does not lie—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Dispute relating to claim of payment of outstanding dues arising from long business transaction is of civil nature which can be decided in civil suit. Criminal proceedings thereon being abuse of the process of the court are quashed. <em>Delwvar Hossain Sowdagar (Alhaj) Vs. The State represented by the Deputy Commissioner Chittagong and others, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 183.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 409/109— Misappropriation by criminal brench of trust</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 5(2)— Offence of criminal misconduct by abuse of official position</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a case where the Minister and the Secretary acted merely on the recommendation of tender committee, they are not liable for any commission of offence, if any, committed by the members of the tender committee. When no offence is disclosed either in the FIR or in the charge sheet, the proceedings initiated thereon being abuse of the process of the court are held by the apex court to have been rightly quashed by the High Court Division.<em>State Vs. Mohammad Nasim and others, 10 MLR (2005) (AD) 213.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 409 and 109— To constitute offence the constituent ingredients must be present—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 5(2)— Punishment for criminal misconduct—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Merely doing some routine work without entrustment of the money in question no offence of abetment is committed—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">To constitute offence punishable under section 409/109 of the Penal Code read with section 5(2) of the Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947, there must be entrustment and dishonest misappropriation of property by abuse of the official power. Mere doing some routine work by way of making entry in cash book of certain amount by the Secretary of Union Parishad under direction of the chairman who enchased the cheque and the money was never entrusted to the convict appellant and there being no evidence of complicity and involvement with the alleged misappropriation or abetment thereof on the part of the convict appellant, the conviction and sentence has been held by the High Court Division as not sustainable in law.<em>Moslem Uddin (Md.) Vs. The State, 10 MLR (2005) (HC) 199.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 409— Charge of Misappropriation—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 5(2)— Criminal Misconduct by Public Servant—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Charge of misappropriation under section 409 of the Penal Code read </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">with section 5(2) of the Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947 has to be established with consistent and cogent evidence in order to secure conviction of accused public servant. In the case of misappropriation in relation to earth work the measurement book is the relevant evidence to establish the charge. When the measurement book is not produced and the evidence so brought on record are discrepant, no conviction in such a case is held to be sustainable.</span> <em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Zahirul Haq (Md.) and another Vs. The State, 7 MLR (2002) (HC) 458.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 418— Making licensing agreement on unsolicited offer does not constitute offence under section 418—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 5(2)—Criminal misconduct— constituent elements—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">When the allegations do not constitute offence under section 418 of the Penal Code read with section 5(2) of the Prevention of Corruption Act the proceedings initiated thereon being abuse of the process of the court are quashed.<em>Mohammad Nasim and another Vs. The State, 9 MLR (2004) (HC) 364.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 420— Ingredients constituting the offence—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">When the offence under section 420 of the Penal Code, 1860 prima facie is disclosed in the petition of complaint the proceedings drawn thereon cannot be quashed under section 561A Cr. P.C. on the plea of the transaction being civil in nature. <em><span style="letter-spacing: -1.0pt;">Fouzia</span> Begum © Rina and others Vs. Md. Azizul Bari and another, 8 MLR (2003) (AD) 63.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"> <br/></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Penal Code, 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">Section 466, 468 and 471— Offence of forgery— Necessary evidence— When not brought on record — Retrial ordered—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';">When the vital documents are not brought on record and marked exhibits and the vital witness are not examined in the face of the offence involving great public importance retrial of the case is directed to comply with the necessary requirements of law. <em>Sirajuddin Sheikh (Md.) Vs. The State, 6 MLR (2001) (HC) 171.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"><strong>Penal Code, 1860—</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Arial Unicode MS';"><strong>Section 468</strong>— Unless the allegation falls within the definition of forgery as defined under section 463, there is</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> no offence constituted as punishable under section 468—In order to be punishable under section 468 of the Penal Code, the allegation must fit in the definition of forgery under section 463. Merely executing a document containing false statements without false personating, does not constitute offence punishable under section 468 of the Penal Code. Ibrahim <em>Ali (Hazi) Vs. The Slate, 7 MLR (2002) (AD) 235.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code 1860—</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sentence- To be proportionate</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Awarding sentence must be proportionate to the nature and gravity of the offence and serve as deterrent to the potential offenders. <em>The State Vs. Ershad Ali Sikdar and others, 8 MLR (2003) (HC) 137.</em></span></p><p> </p></div></div>
